< Text>
My eyes got weary and my head went light on the way to "Hotel California" and I had to find a place to stay.
Clean, comfortable and convenient describes this place. I met the coolest guy on the whole trip "I assume Tom by reading the reviews". Took my wife and infant in for the night rested up and kept a good memorable experience. Thanks guys, manager, cleaning staff and the pple staying there.
I couldn't have made it another minute on the road 5hat night and I called in, no rez and the guy put us up without the nickel and dime.
This was the only non corporate hotel on the whole trip from Cleveland to Bakersfield and I would choose it anytime for the next run!!!

Thanks guys EXCELLENT SERVICE!<//Text>

- TAKE NOTE OF TYPICAL SALES TACTICS. They will push and not clearly explain to you what is really going on with the transaction.  If you feel uncomfortable about the experience, decline and leave the store or call T-Mobile customer service right at the store and ask them about any questions that you have.

- READ EVERYTHING BEFORE YOU SIGN.  They purposely print your contract and receipt in small fine print by scaling 4 pages into one.  Other T-Mobile store either do 1 or 2 so it is readable.  The associate will then proceed to flip through everything and ask you to sign at the end.

- Go home and reread the contract again and check your account online to see if there is anything out of the ordinary.  There is a restocking fee for phones but all other items can be return for a full refund.</text>

charles chiles< /username>
< Review>
It was my first visit to Subway at 124 Loma Sante Fe, Ste.101. It was just a short walk from the Solana Beach Amtrack/Coaster and Breeze Transit Station.
This Subway Store is part of a small shopping complex however, it's easy to see from Old Highway 101, which parallels most of San Diego's  famed "North County" surfing beaches!
There were four of us in our party and we had just come from a day at the Del Mar Fair and we spotted the Subway from the train station's upper  street level.
What a neat looking little store. I hadn't been to any Subway Stores for over a year, as the food that I ordered at the last store in the inner city just didn't hit the spot.
This Subway was so cool; it was about 18:50 pm
and  we had their store all to ourselves. I ordered a 6" B.M.T. Sub and it 30 oz fountain coke; my
Italian B.M.T. was really awesome! I was really impressed, as I always watch how my sandwiches are made and I think that the guy who prepared it, added a couple extra pieces of ham to my sandwich. I also like them toasted, because it melts the cheese on my sub.
My friends ordered the Ft.Long Fave; a 12" ham sub, with chips and a couple of 30oz. fountain drinks too.
I'm primarily a vegetarian but, Subway touts it's sandwiches as healthy food and after our meal at
this Solana Beach Subway, I couldn't agree more!
Mine was simply delicious and I loved it; my friends felt the same way about their meals.
This Subway-it was early Sunday evening-was quite cozy.
The associates who worked there were most gracious and I honestly felt that they were there for us.
In fact, the whole senario is what had brought me back to Subway! If I owned a car, I'd surely be "a frequent flyer" and I drive all the way up to Solana  Beach, just there!
I don't care what the Subway commercials say and eventhough they are a "chain store,"
my customer service experiences aren't always the same, just because the store name is the same.
Anyhow, whenever I crave a good healthy sub sandwich, I'll now keep Subway on my mind as healthy alternative.
Some food for thought: Many Californian's are really cheap tippers and you can take that anyway you please; most of the associates who work at these stores make only Federal Minimum Wage and in some states, it's as low as $8.50 an hour, while here in California, for most, it starts at $11 an hour and is going up about a dollar a year until it reaches $15.
San Diego's living costs are amongst the highest in the nation, which is something for you to think about next time you dine out...
And don't forget to eat at Subway!</Review>

< Rating>
5</Rating>
<Text>It's in the front lobby of the hotel and connected to a bar which you can buy drinks from either place. Not much privacy because as you sit closer to the bar area its loud and if you sit close to the lobby there is traffic. So pick your poison. Greeted instantly and seated promptly after. Even got to pick my seat. Waitress was very pleasant so no complaints there. So now about the main course. Alright so...if you are afraid to spend money do not come here. The trend now with "foodies" is they want the food cheap and they want alot of it. I wanted sushi and the closest one to walking distance from my hotel happened to be this one. Yes I too was skeptical of the reviews but no pun intended went with my gut. Whenever I try a new sushi spot they have to have either 1. Omakase or 2. A Sashimi style with at least 5 varieties of fish. This is a baseline I use to decide if eating here is worth it or not. I expect no fishy smell or taste. I also expect the most basic of fish like salmon to be buttery and creamy. Your hotate better be extremely delicate and slightly sweet. Any bluefin tuna (the major three) should be prepped with extreme diligence. Now for me I have had sushi from Japan, Hawaii, other California spots, and to the midwest. Yes this place is on the pricier side and I believe it's mostly to do with being in a hotel so honestly for me it was not half bad as to what I paid for. So yes the Sashimi variety passed with flying colors. Now it was onto a roll. There are two things I care about when it comes to rolls is proportion and taste. If you have too much rice...over it. If the fried ebi is hot, cold, soggy, or hard as a rock in the roll...nope. if you top heavy it with fish...negative. Nothing should overpower each other. Yes the roll was $19 dollars but the sushi chef (pretty sure they have not earned Itamae status) hit both proportion and taste just right with the exception of getting a little crazy with the sauce on the plate...which is fine because it looks pretty and you can choose to apply more or less on your bite. Another pet peeve of mine is timing. With sushi timing matters alot because the Sashimi or sushi should be just below room temperature. If it's cold you know they do not know how to prepare the sushi or trying to mask the taste of the fish. Also the sushi chef should be mindful of when you order, finish, and when to give your next plate. If you wait too long its poor service or the sushi may get too warm. If you are not done and get served your next plate your sushi will sit longer than it should. In this case they served it with perfect timing. Once I was done with my Sashimi I was served the roll.  Does it have a michelin  star, no but as a hotel lobby sushi spot that is pretty darn good for me gets my five stars.<//Text>< pics>
None<//pics>

<time>1606104244900< /time><Rating>5< /Rating>< review>
I have visited Marlowe twice now and had a great experience both times! They've implemented new COVID protocols (temp check, questions at the door, etc.) and put in plastic partitions at the manicure stations, so I felt perfectly safe going in for both a mani and pedi. I first got the Marlowe Mani and had Aiden as my nail technician. He was really great! I'm really pleased with how my nails turned out (smooth, shiny with beautiful shaping and cuticle work!).

The interior of the salon is super chic and clean. The staff were all incredibly friendly and attentive. I didn't have to wait to get started upon arrival. I also really appreciate the ethical practices of this business. A living wage is SO essential, and the quality of the service matches the price in my opinion.

I got my first Marlowe Pedi today. It was divine! I had Thi as my technician. She was wonderful. She really took the time to attend to the little details. My feet were a mess before a went in since I'm a dancer: lots of dead skin and calluses. She was both gentle and thorough as she attended to the bottoms of my feet, cuticles and areas around the nails. My feet look and feel great now! She even put my flip flops back on my feet for me when it was time to check out so that I wouldn't accidentally mess up my toenails. So sweet! I'd highly recommend Marlowe if you're looking for some high quality pampering.< /review>

<username>Yasyn Knight< /username><Date>1574628529103</Date><Rating>5</Rating>< Review>
Clean and beautiful looking nail salon. They keep it simple and clean here. It's comforting to see a package of clean tools being opened before you. One of my biggest fears is a fungal infection from going to a salon so I've painted my own nails for many years. My partner booked me a manicure here for a special occasion. I brought my own nail color here, which is ZOYA brand and they have the basecoat and topcoat to match. They have a lot of ZOYA and OPI from what I can remember.

The staff is very friendly, welcoming. The place doesn't smell crazy like most nail salons since this place doesn't do acrylic or other heavier chemical processes. They don't have too many stations so I was asked to sit at the waiting area while my nails dried, which was fine. I think the music playing can get a bit overwhelming because it's high energy, but that's just me, I'm a quiet introverted person.

They have drying drops at the very end, which I've never used before. I was told to wait at least 1 hour for my manicure to dry before doing anything more intensive with my hands.

The person who worked on my nails was pretty quiet, but did a good job. I think I am just not used to my cuticles being cleaned up and pushed back so that is always a sensitive process for me. I did notice they felt dry the days afterwards, and a pit peely, so moisturizing the following days was a must.

I think the only criticism isn't heavy, but I do think I could have done a better job at the actual nail painting portion. There was some pooling at the cuticles. I thought at least a brush with acetone could be used to clean up the cuticles for a clean line, but maybe it has something to do with using new tools every time, so that's ok. I understand the nail professional needs to get through each client efficiently so they don't have all day to paint perfectly.

Overall a good experience. :)<//Review>

I made the reservation the day prior IN person and initially, the receptionist seemed friendly/accommodating. She said she was able to get us in together for a manicure but our pedicures would be staggered, one after the other. I handed over my credit card and reserved our appointments.

We arrived to the appointment and told the receptionist that we were there for a mani/pedi. As we were picking out our colors she informs me that we are only booked for manicures, in an accusatory tone. I told her no, I most certainly booked both and we had had a discussion about how long the services would be with them staggered.

We are seated and the receptionist comes back over and says again that its not on the schedule and she isn't sure what happened, that it must have been booked on a different day, but they are fully booked and can only do our manicures. Meanwhile, she keeps going back to the front desk to speak to another woman with her back turned (the manager/owner) and relaying everything I am saying to her. This is only a few feet away, so I can hear everything. The owner/manager never once turned around to acknowledge me and never came over to apologize for their error. From what I could overhear, she had a very "oh well" attitude.

Our mani appt was at 2pm. Their best offer was to do a single pedicure at 6pm and acted as if they were bending over backwards for this to work. Mind you, there is only one other person in the salon, mid manicure when we had arrived. No - I have a baby and I can't wait around for four hours to get a pedicure, this was already an effort to get time away. I asked if I could just shorten my manicure and get a quick file/polish change on my toes. As a new mother herself (the owner was outside with her infant when we got there) this is something I would think would resonate with her.
